# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Task: Analyze Test Coverage Gaps in Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

**Repository:** envoyproxy/envoy
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Envoy's HTTP Connection Manager (HCM) filter chain implementation. The HCM is the core HTTP processing pipeline in Envoy, responsible for routing, filter execution, and response handling.

## Scope

Focus on the HCM implementation in `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` and its test file `test/common/http/conn_manager_impl_test.cc`. Also consider:
- `source/common/http/filter_manager.cc` — filter chain execution
- `source/common/http/header_map_impl.cc` — header manipulation

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific untested code paths** in the HCM (with file + approximate line references)
2. **Propose a concrete test case** for each gap (test name, setup, assertions)
3. **Explain why each gap matters** (what bugs could slip through)
4. **Prioritize by risk**: label each gap as HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md` with this structure:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary
[Brief overview of the most critical gaps found]

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: [Title]
- **File**: source/common/http/...
- **Lines**: ~NNN-NNN
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Description**: [What code path is untested]
- **Proposed Test**: [Test name and approach]
- **Why It Matters**: [Potential bugs if untested]

[Repeat for gaps 2-5+]

## File References
[List of key files analyzed]
```

## Anti-Requirements
- Do not fabricate file paths or function names — inspect the actual codebase
- Do not list gaps without proposing concrete test cases

The analysis is complete. Here's a summary of what was written to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`:

## Coverage Gap Analysis — Envoy HCM

Five specific untested code paths were identified by cross-referencing the implementation against the full test suite (conn_manager_impl_test.cc, _test_2.cc, _test_3.cc, conn_manager_misc_test.cc):

---

**Gap 1 (HIGH) — `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` / `isPrematureRstStream` (~lines 677–748)**
The entire premature-reset detection system is completely untested. Every relevant identifier (`downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_`, `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey`, `number_premature_stream_resets_`, `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) returned zero hits across all test files. This mechanism defends against RST flood attacks by closing connections that exceed a premature-reset ratio — bugs here could silently disable that defense or cause recursive `doConnectionClose` stack overflows.

**Gap 2 (HIGH) — Non-graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` (~lines 797–824)**
Only `sendGoAwayAndClose(true)` is tested (`SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful`). The non-graceful path that immediately sends `shutdownNotice()` + `goAway()` then calls `doConnectionClose("forced_goaway")` is untested, as is the `go_away_sent_` idempotency guard. A regression could cause double-close or skip the GOAWAY entirely.

**Gap 3 (MEDIUM) — `validateTrailers` → `handleCodecError` connection close (~lines 1295–1297)**
Existing UHV trailer tests verify the 400 response or stream reset but never mock `streamErrorOnInvalidHttpMessage()` to return `false`. The path that closes the entire connection via `handleCodecError()` when stream-level errors are disabled is never verified — a regression here leaves HTTP/1.1 connections open after a rejected trailer, enabling request smug
... (truncated)

The most critical is the **premature reset detection and\nconnection-draining system** (`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`), which\nimplements a security-adjacent mechanism with no unit test coverage whatsoever. The second critical\ngap is the **non-graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` path**, where only the graceful variant is\ntested. Three additional medium-risk gaps cover route-level buffer limit adjustment, trailer\nvalidation connection-close behavior, and an HTTP/2 edge case in connection duration timeout\nhandling.\n\n---\n\n## Coverage Gaps\n\n### Gap 1: Premature Reset Detection and Connection Draining\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~677\u2013748 (`isPrematureRstStream`, `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**\n\n`doDeferredStreamDestroy()` calls `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` on every stream teardown.\nThis function maintains two connection-level counters:\n\n- `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` \u2014 total non-internal stream completions\n- `number_premature_stream_resets_` \u2014 streams that completed before a response code was set and\n  within the configured minimum lifetime (`PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey`, default 1 s)\n\nWhen the ratio `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`\n(or `>= limit` at the threshold), the connection is aborted with detail `too_many_premature_resets`\nand `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is incremented. A `drained_due_to_premature_resets_`\nflag prevents recursive connection-close storms. The companion `isPrematureRstStream()` function\n(lines 677\u2013698) determines whether each individual stream counts as \"premature.\"\n\nSearches for every relevant identifier (`isPrematureRstStream`, `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`,\n`downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_`, `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey`,\n`PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey`, `number_premature_stream_resets_`,\n`drained_due_to_premature_resets_`) across all test files returned **zero results**. This entire\nsubsystem has no unit test coverage.\n\n**Proposed Test**: `TEST_F(HttpConnectionManagerImplTest, PrematureResetDetectionDrainsConnection)`\n\nSetup:\n1. Configure `PrematureResetTotalStreamCountKey` runtime value to 4 (low threshold for the test).\n2. Configure `PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey` to 1.\n3. Bugs in the threshold arithmetic (off-by-one in the `* 2` comparison at\nlines 731 and 735), the recursion guard, or the `isPrematureRstStream` lifetime check could:\n\n- Fail to drain the connection under a genuine attack (security regression).\n- Drain legitimate connections where resets are incidental (availability regression).\n- Cause an infinite recursion / stack overflow in `doConnectionClose` \u2192 `resetAllStreams` \u2192\n  `onResetStream` \u2192 `doDeferredStreamDestroy` \u2192 `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` if the\n  `drained_due_to_premature_resets_` guard were accidentally removed.\n\n---\n\n### Gap 2: Non-Graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` Path\n\n- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`\n- **Lines**: ~797\u2013824 (`sendGoAwayAndClose`)\n- **Risk**: HIGH\n\n**Description**\n\n`sendGoAwayAndClose` has two branches based on the `graceful` boolean argument:\n\n- `graceful=true` (lines 808\u2013815): starts the drain sequence, sets `go_away_sent_ = true`.\n- `graceful=false` (lines 816\u2013823): immediately calls `codec_->shutdownNotice()`, `codec_->goAway()`,\n  `go_away_sent_ = true`, then `doConnectionClose(FlushWriteAndDelay, ...)` with detail\n  `\"forced_goaway\"`.\n\nThe existing test `SendGoAwayAndCloseGraceful` (conn_manager_impl_test.cc:5263) covers only\n`graceful=true`. # Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Envoy HTTP Connection Manager

## Summary

Analysis of `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc` (2,608 lines) against its test files
(`conn_manager_impl_test.cc`, `_test_2.cc`, `_test_3.cc`, `conn_manager_misc_test.cc`) reveals
five specific untested code paths. The most critical is the **premature reset detection and
connection-draining system** (`maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets` + `isPrematureRstStream`), which
implements a security-adjacent mechanism with no unit test coverage whatsoever. The second critical
gap is the **non-graceful `sendGoAwayAndClose(false)` path**, where only the graceful variant is
tested. Three additional medium-risk gaps cover route-level buffer limit adjustment, trailer
validation connection-close behavior, and an HTTP/2 edge case in connection duration timeout
handling.

---

## Coverage Gaps

### Gap 1: Premature Reset Detection and Connection Draining

- **File**: `source/common/http/conn_manager_impl.cc`
- **Lines**: ~677–748 (`isPrematureRstStream`, `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets`)
- **Risk**: HIGH

**Description**

`doDeferredStreamDestroy()` calls `maybeDrainDueToPrematureResets()` on every stream teardown.
This function maintains two connection-level counters:

- `closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_` — total non-internal stream completions
- `number_premature_stream_resets_` — streams that completed before a response code was set and
  within the configured minimum lifetime (`PrematureResetMinStreamLifetimeSecondsKey`, default 1 s)

When the ratio `number_premature_stream_resets_ * 2 >= closed_non_internally_destroyed_requests_`
(or `>= limit` at the threshold), the connection is aborted with detail `too_many_premature_resets`
and `downstream_rq_too_many_premature_resets_` is incremented. A `draine
... (truncated)
